(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-left{float:left;clear:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-right{float:right;clear:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-clear-left{float:left;clear:left;margin-right:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-clear-right{float:right;clear:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-left{float:left;margin-right:1em}.mw-parser-output .stack-margin-right{float:right;margin-left:1em}}</style><div class="stack stack-right"><div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_(2).jpg"><img alt="Twelve men in black suits stand talking in small groups under a backdrop with the words Lisbonne and Lisboa." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="654" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg/220px-NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg/330px-NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg/440px-NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NATO_and_US_EU_Summits_in_Lisbon_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former American President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> with former Turkish President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdullah_Gul" title="Abdullah Gul">Abdullah Gul</a> and other leaders at the NATO Summit in Lisbon in November 2010</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>NATO has thirty members, mainly in Europe and North America. Some of these countries also have territory on multiple continents, which can be covered only as far south as the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a> in the Atlantic Ocean, which defines NATO's "area of responsibility" under Article 6 of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a>. During the original treaty negotiations, the United States insisted that colonies such as the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a> be excluded from the treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins2011122–123_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins2011122–123-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">French Algeria</a> was, however, covered until <a href="/wiki/1962_Algerian_independence_referendum" title="1962 Algerian independence referendum">its independence</a> on 3 July 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Twelve of these thirty are original members who joined in 1949, while the other eighteen joined in one of eight enlargement rounds.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Few members spend more than two percent of their gross domestic product on defence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> with the United States accounting for three quarters of NATO defence spending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_arrangements">Special arrangements</span></h3>
<p>The three Nordic countries which joined NATO as founding members, Denmark, Iceland, and Norway, chose to limit their participation in three areas: there would be no permanent peacetime bases, no nuclear warheads and no Allied military activity (unless invited) permitted on their territory. However, Denmark allowed the U.S. Air Force to maintain an existing base, <a href="/wiki/Thule_Air_Base" title="Thule Air Base">Thule Air Base</a>, in Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the mid-1960s to the mid-1990s, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> pursued a military strategy of independence from NATO under a policy dubbed "Gaullo-Mitterrandism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> negotiated the return of France to the integrated military command and the Defence Planning Committee in 2009, the latter being disbanded the following year. France remains the only NATO member outside the Nuclear Planning Group and unlike the United States and the United Kingdom, will not commit its nuclear-armed submarines to the alliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP-France_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-WP-France-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian-france_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-france-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlargement">Enlargement</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO" title="Enlargement of NATO">Enlargement of NATO</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1034237262" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="stack stack-right"><div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg"><img alt="A map of Europe with countries labelled in shades of blue, green, and yellow based on when they joined NATO." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg/220px-History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg/330px-History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg/440px-History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:History_of_NATO_enlargement.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NATO has added 14 new members since <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> and the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Accession to the alliance is governed with individual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Membership_Action_Plan" title="Membership Action Plan">Membership Action Plans</a>, and requires approval by each current member. NATO currently has three candidate countries that are in the process of joining the alliance: <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>. <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> is the most recent state to sign an accession protocol to become a NATO member state, which it did in February 2019 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accession_of_North_Macedonia_to_NATO" title="Accession of North Macedonia to NATO">became a member state</a> on 27 March 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Its accession had been blocked by Greece for many years due to the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">Macedonia naming dispute</a>, which was resolved in 2018 by the <a href="/wiki/Prespa_agreement" title="Prespa agreement">Prespa agreement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In order to support each other in the process, new and potential members in the region formed the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Charter" title="Adriatic Charter">Adriatic Charter</a> in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> was also named as an aspiring member, and was promised "future membership" during the 2008 summit in Bucharest,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> though in 2014, US President Barack Obama said the country was not "currently on a path" to membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Obama_says_no_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Obama_says_no-118">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Ukraine–NATO relations">relationship with NATO</a> and Europe has been politically controversial, and improvement of these relations was one of the goals of the "<a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a>" protests that saw the ousting of pro-Russian President <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> in 2014. Ukraine is one of eight countries in Eastern Europe with an <a href="/wiki/Individual_Partnership_Action_Plan" title="Individual Partnership Action Plan">Individual Partnership Action Plan</a>. IPAPs began in 2002, and are open to countries that have the political will and ability to deepen their relationship with NATO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> On 21 February 2019, the Constitution of Ukraine was amended, the norms on the strategic course of Ukraine for membership in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and NATO are enshrined in the preamble of the Basic Law, three articles and transitional provisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> At the June <a href="/wiki/2021_Brussels_summit" title="2021 Brussels summit">2021 Brussels Summit</a>, NATO leaders reiterated the decision taken at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Bucharest_summit" title="2008 Bucharest summit">2008 Bucharest Summit</a> that Ukraine would become a member of the Alliance with the Membership Action Plan (MAP) as an integral part of the process and Ukraine's right to determine its own future and foreign policy course without outside interference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-121">[121]</a></sup> On 30 November 2021, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> stated that an expansion of NATO's presence in Ukraine, especially the deployment of any <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">long-range missiles</a> capable of striking Russian cities or <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_missile_defense" title="United States national missile defense">missile defence systems</a> similar to those in Romania and Poland, would be a "red line" issue for Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Putin asked U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> for legal guarantees that NATO would not expand eastward or put "weapons systems that threaten us in close vicinity to Russian territory."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> NATO Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Jens_Stoltenberg" title="Jens Stoltenberg">Jens Stoltenberg</a> replied that "It's only Ukraine and 30 NATO allies that decide when Ukraine is ready to join NATO. Russia has no veto, Russia has no say, and Russia has no right to establish a sphere of influence to try to control their neighbors."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Russia continued to politically oppose further expansion, seeing it as inconsistent with informal understandings between Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> and European and US negotiators that allowed for a peaceful German reunification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spiegel_review_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel_review-128">[128]</a></sup> NATO's expansion efforts are often seen by Moscow leaders as a continuation of a Cold War attempt to surround and isolate Russia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> though they have also been criticized in the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Art1998_383_to_384_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Art1998_383_to_384-130">[130]</a></sup> A June 2016 <a href="/wiki/Levada_Center" title="Levada Center">Levada</a> poll found that 68 percent of Russians think that deploying NATO troops in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> – former Eastern bloc countries bordering Russia – is a threat to Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> In contrast, 65 percent of Poles surveyed in a 2017 Pew Research Center report identified Russia as a "major threat", with an average of 31 percent saying so across all NATO countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> and 67 percent of Poles surveyed in 2018 favour US forces being based in Poland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Of non-<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> Eastern European countries surveyed by Gallup in 2016, all but <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> were more likely than not to view NATO as a protective alliance rather than a threat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> A 2006 study in the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Security_Studies_(journal)" title="Security Studies (journal)">Security Studies</a></i> argued that NATO enlargement contributed to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_consolidation" title="Democratic consolidation">democratic consolidation</a> in Central and Eastern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> also opposes further expansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Following_Russia.27s_2022_invasion_of_Ukraine"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Following_Russia's_2022_invasion_of_Ukraine">Following Russia's 2022 invasion of Ukraine</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_(51905505001).jpg"><img alt="A crowd of people in winter coats march past a white domed church above a set of snowy stairs, some carrying signs and blue and yellow Ukrainian flags." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5534" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_%2851905505001%29.jpg/220px-We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_%2851905505001%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_%2851905505001%29.jpg/330px-We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_%2851905505001%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_%2851905505001%29.jpg/440px-We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_%2851905505001%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:We_Stand_with_Ukraine_2022_Helsinki_-_Finland_(51905505001).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protestors at a February 2022 rally against <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russia's invasion of Ukraine</a> march past the statue of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia" title="Alexander II of Russia">Alexander II</a> in <a href="/wiki/Senate_Square,_Helsinki" title="Senate Square, Helsinki">Senate Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a></div></div></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>, public opinion in <a href="/wiki/Finland%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Finland–NATO relations">Finland</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Sweden%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Sweden–NATO relations">Sweden</a> swung sharply in favor of joining NATO, with more citizens supporting NATO membership than those who were opposed to it for the first time. A poll on 30 March 2022 revealed that about 61% of Finns were in favor of NATO membership, as opposed to 16% against and 23% uncertain. A poll on 1 April revealed that about 51% of Swedes were in favor of NATO membership, as opposed to 27% against.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Finland_and_Sweden_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Finland_and_Sweden-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurtling_towards_NATO_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-hurtling_towards_NATO-138">[138]</a></sup> In mid-April, the governments of Finland and Sweden began exploring NATO membership, with their governments commissioning security reports on this subject.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The addition of the two Nordic countries would significantly expand NATO's capabilities in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic</a>, and Baltic regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Going_Nordic_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Going_Nordic-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 May 2022, the Finnish government announced that it would apply for NATO membership, subject to approval by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">country's parliament</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> which voted 188–8 in favor of the move on 17 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Swedish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Andersson" title="Magdalena Andersson">Magdalena Andersson</a> announced her country would apply for NATO membership on 17 May,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> and both Finland and Sweden formally submitted applications for NATO membership on 18 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fin-swe-appliction_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-fin-swe-appliction-145">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> voiced opposition to Finland and Sweden joining NATO, accusing the two countries of providing support to the <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers%27_Party" title="Kurdistan Workers' Party">Kurdistan Workers' Party</a> (PKK) and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Defense_Units" title="People's Defense Units">People's Defense Units</a> (YPG), two Kurdish groups which Turkey has designated as terrorist organizations. On <span data-sort-value="000000002022-06-28-0000" style="white-space:nowrap">28 June</span>, at a NATO summit in Madrid, Turkey agreed to support the membership bids of Finland and Sweden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turkey.finland.sweden.reuters_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-turkey.finland.sweden.reuters-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turkey.finland.sweden.sky_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-turkey.finland.sweden.sky-147">[147]</a></sup> On 5 July, the 30 NATO ambassadors signed off on the accession protocols for Sweden and Finland and formally approved the decisions of the NATO summit on 28 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> This must be ratified by the various governments; as of 27 September, all countries except Hungary and Turkey had ratified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NATO_Defense_Expenditure_Budget">NATO Defense Expenditure Budget</span></h3>
<p>The increase in the number of NATO members over the years hasn’t been sustained by an increase in the defense expenditures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Being concerned about the decreasing defense budgets and aiming to improve financial equity commitments and boost the effectiveness of financial expenditure, NATO members met at the 2014 Wales Summit to establish the Defense Investment Pledge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Members considered it necessary to contribute at least 2% of their Gross Domestic Product (<a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>) to defense and 20% of their defense budget to major equipment which includes allocations to defense research and development by 2024.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>The implementation of the Defense Investment Pledge is hindered by the lack of legal binding obligation by the members, European Union fiscal laws, member states’ domestic public expenditure priorities, and political willingness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> In 2021, eight member states achieved the goal of 2% GDP contribution to defense spending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> In 2020, 18 NATO members were able to reach the target of 20% contribution to major equipment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The improvements in the compliance with the Wales recommendations are facilitated by the increasing risk to the security of the members posed by the Russian Federation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships_with_third_countries">Partnerships with third countries</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_NATO" title="Foreign relations of NATO">Foreign relations of NATO</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg"><img alt="Hundreds of soldiers in military uniforms stand behind a line on a tarmac with 14 flags held by individuals at the front." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1588" data-file-width="2504" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg/220px-Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg/330px-Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg/440px-Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cooperative_Archer_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Partnership for Peace conducts multinational military exercises like Cooperative Archer, which took place in Tbilisi in July 2007 with 500 servicemen from four NATO members, eight PfP members, and Jordan, a Mediterranean Dialogue participant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> (PfP) programme was established in 1994 and is based on individual bilateral relations between each partner country and NATO: each country may choose the extent of its participation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pfp_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-pfp-160">[160]</a></sup> Members include all current and former members of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a> (EAPC) was first established on 29 May 1997, and is a forum for regular coordination, consultation and dialogue between all fifty participants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The PfP programme is considered the operational wing of the Euro-Atlantic Partnership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pfp_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-pfp-160">[160]</a></sup> Other third countries also have been contacted for participation in some activities of the PfP framework such as Afghanistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) signed a comprehensive package of arrangements with NATO under the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Plus_agreement" title="Berlin Plus agreement">Berlin Plus agreement</a> on 16 December 2002. With this agreement, the EU was given the possibility of using NATO assets in case it wanted to act independently in an international crisis, on the condition that NATO itself did not want to act – the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Right_of_first_refusal" title="Right of first refusal">right of first refusal</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> For example, Article 42(7) of the 1982 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> specifies that "If a Member State is the victim of armed aggression on its territory, the other Member States shall have towards it an obligation of aid and assistance by all the means in their power". The treaty applies globally to specified territories whereas NATO is restricted under its Article 6 to operations north of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>. It provides a "double framework" for the EU countries that are also linked with the PfP programme.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Additionally, NATO cooperates and discusses its activities with numerous other non-NATO members. The <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Dialogue" title="Mediterranean Dialogue">Mediterranean Dialogue</a> was established in 1994 to coordinate in a similar way with <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Israel" title="Foreign relations of Israel">Israel</a> and countries in North Africa. The <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Cooperation_Initiative" title="Istanbul Cooperation Initiative">Istanbul Cooperation Initiative</a> was announced in 2004 as a dialogue forum for the Middle East along the same lines as the Mediterranean Dialogue. The four participants are also linked through the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> In June 2018, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> expressed its wish to join NATO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> However, NATO declined membership, stating that only additional European countries could join according to <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_NATO#Article_10_and_the_Open_Door_Policy" title="Enlargement of NATO">Article 10 of NATO's founding treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Qatar and NATO have previously signed a security agreement together in January 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup>
</p><p>Political dialogue with Japan began in 1990, and since then, the Alliance has gradually increased its contact with countries that do not form part of any of these cooperation initiatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> In 1998, NATO established a set of general guidelines that do not allow for a formal institutionalization of relations, but reflect the Allies' desire to increase cooperation. Following extensive debate, the term "Contact Countries" was agreed by the Allies in 2000. By 2012, the Alliance had broadened this group, which meets to discuss issues such as counter-piracy and technology exchange, under the names "partners across the globe" or "global partners".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gao_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-gao-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, both contact countries, are also members of the <a href="/wiki/AUSCANNZUKUS" title="AUSCANNZUKUS">AUSCANNZUKUS</a> strategic alliance, and similar regional or bilateral agreements between contact countries and NATO members also aid cooperation. NATO Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Jens_Stoltenberg" title="Jens Stoltenberg">Jens Stoltenberg</a> stated that NATO needs to "address the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Century" title="Chinese Century">rise of China</a>," by closely cooperating with Australia, New Zealand, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombia_and_NATO" title="Colombia and NATO">Colombia</a> is NATO's latest partner and Colombia has access to the full range of cooperative activities NATO offers to partners; Colombia became the first and only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American" title="Latin American">Latin American</a> country to cooperate with NATO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Structure_of_NATO" title="Structure of NATO">Structure of NATO</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=NATO&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2037" data-file-width="3683" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/220px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/330px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg/440px-NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NATO_Ministers_of_Defense_and_of_Foreign_Affairs_meet_at_NATO_headquarters_in_Brussels_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The North Atlantic Council convening in 2010 with a defence/foreign minister configuration</div></div></div>
<p>All agencies and organizations of NATO are integrated into either the civilian administrative or military executive roles. For the most part they perform roles and functions that directly or indirectly support the security role of the alliance as a whole.
</p><p>The civilian structure includes:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Council" title="North Atlantic Council">North Atlantic Council</a> (NAC) is the body which has effective governance authority and powers of decision in NATO, consisting of member states' permanent representatives or representatives at higher level (ministers of foreign affairs or defence, or heads of state or government). The NAC convenes at least once a week and takes major decisions regarding NATO's policies. The meetings of the North Atlantic Council are chaired by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_NATO" title="Secretary General of NATO">secretary general</a> and, when decisions have to be made, action is agreed upon by consensus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> There is no voting or decision by majority. Each nation represented at the Council table or on any of its subordinate committees retains complete sovereignty and responsibility for its own decisions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Headquarters" title="NATO Headquarters">NATO Headquarters</a>, located on Boulevard Léopold III/Leopold III-laan, B-1110 Brussels, which is in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brussels_(municipality)" title="Brussels (municipality)">City of Brussels</a> municipality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> The staff at the Headquarters is composed of national delegations of member countries and includes civilian and military liaison offices and officers or diplomatic missions and diplomats of partner countries, as well as the International Staff and International Military Staff filled from serving members of the armed forces of member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Non-governmental groups have also grown up in support of NATO, broadly under the banner of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Council" title="Atlantic Council">Atlantic Council</a>/<a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Treaty_Association" title="Atlantic Treaty Association">Atlantic Treaty Association</a> movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paper_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paper-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></li></ul>

href="/wiki/File:NATO_laea_location_map.svg" title="File:NATO laea location map.svg">class=notpageimage| </a></div>Locations of <a class="mw-selflink selflink">NATO</a>'s two strategic commands—<a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Transformation" title="Allied Command Transformation">Allied Command Transformation</a> (ACT; yellow marks) and <a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Operations" title="Allied Command Operations">Allied Command Operations</a> (ACO; red marks)—the latter of which has <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Powers_Europe" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe">Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe</a> (SHAPE) as its headquarters. The subordinate centres of ACT and subordinate commands and joint force commands of ACO are also shown. <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:NATO_commands" title="Template:NATO commands"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:NATO_commands" title="Template talk:NATO commands"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:NATO_commands&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></div></div></div>
<p>The military structure includes:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/NATO_Military_Committee" title="NATO Military Committee">Military Committee</a> (MC) is the body of NATO that is composed of <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO" title="Member states of NATO">member states</a>' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_of_Defence" title="Chief of Defence">Chiefs of Defence</a> (CHOD) and advises the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Council" title="North Atlantic Council">North Atlantic Council</a> (NAC) on military policy and strategy. The national CHODs are regularly represented in the MC by their permanent Military Representatives (MilRep), who often are two- or three-star flag officers. Like the council, from time to time the Military Committee also meets at a higher level, namely at the level of Chiefs of Defence, the most senior military officer in each nation's armed forces. The MC is led by its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_NATO_Military_Committee" title="Chairman of the NATO Military Committee">chairman</a>, who directs NATO's military operations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Until 2008 the Military Committee excluded France, due to that country's 1966 decision to remove itself from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Military_Command_Structure" title="NATO Military Command Structure">NATO Military Command Structure</a>, which it rejoined in 1995. Until France rejoined NATO, it was not represented on the Defence Planning Committee, and this led to conflicts between it and NATO members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Such was the case in the lead up to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Iraqi_Freedom" title="Operation Iraqi Freedom">Operation Iraqi Freedom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> The operational work of the committee is supported by the International Military Staff</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Powers_Europe" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe">Allied Command Operations</a> (ACO) is the NATO command responsible for NATO operations worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>
<ul><li>The Rapid Deployable Corps include <a href="/wiki/Eurocorps" title="Eurocorps">Eurocorps</a>, <a href="/wiki/I._German/Dutch_Corps" title="I. German/Dutch Corps">I. German/Dutch Corps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multinational_Corps_Northeast" title="Multinational Corps Northeast">Multinational Corps Northeast</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Rapid_Deployable_Italian_Corps" title="NATO Rapid Deployable Italian Corps">NATO Rapid Deployable Italian Corps</a> among others, as well as naval High Readiness Forces (HRFs), which all report to Allied Command Operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Transformation" title="Allied Command Transformation">Allied Command Transformation</a> (ACT), responsible for transformation and training of NATO forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The organizations and agencies of NATO include:
</p>
<ul><li>Headquarters for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Support_Agency" title="NATO Support Agency">NATO Support Agency</a> will be in Capellen Luxembourg (site of the current NATO Maintenance and Supply Agency – NAMSA).</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/NATO_Communications_and_Information_Agency" title="NATO Communications and Information Agency">NATO Communications and Information Agency</a> Headquarters will be in Brussels, as will the very small staff which will design the new NATO Procurement Agency.</li>
<li>A new <a href="/wiki/NATO_Science_and_Technology_Organization" title="NATO Science and Technology Organization">NATO Science and Technology Organization</a> will be created before July 2012, consisting of Chief Scientist, a Programme Office for Collaborative S&amp;T, and the NATO Undersea Research Centre (NURC).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>The NATO Standardization Agency became the <a href="/wiki/NATO_Standardization_Office" title="NATO Standardization Office">NATO Standardization Office</a> (NSO) in July 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/NATO_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="NATO Parliamentary Assembly">NATO Parliamentary Assembly</a> (NATO PA) is a body that sets broad strategic goals for NATO, which meets at two session per year. NATO PA interacts directly with the parliamentary structures of the national governments of the member states which appoint Permanent Members, or ambassadors to NATO. The NATO Parliamentary Assembly is made up of legislators from the member countries of the North Atlantic Alliance as well as thirteen associate members. It is however officially a structure different from NATO, and has as aim to join deputies of NATO countries in order to discuss security policies on the NATO Council.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_authority_of_NATO_commanders">Legal authority of NATO commanders</span></h3>
<p>NATO is an alliance of 30 sovereign nations and their individual sovereignty is unaffected by participation in the alliance. NATO has no parliaments, no laws, no enforcement, and no power to punish individual citizens. As a consequence of this lack of sovereignty the power and authority of a NATO commander are limited. NATO commanders cannot punish offences such as failure to obey a lawful order; dereliction of duty; or disrespect to a senior officer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-terla_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-terla-185">[185]</a></sup> NATO commanders expect obeisance but sometimes need to subordinate their desires or plans to the operators who are themselves subject to sovereign codes of conduct like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UCMJ" title="UCMJ">UCMJ</a>. A case in point was the clash between General <a href="/wiki/Mike_Jackson_(British_Army_officer)" title="Mike Jackson (British Army officer)">Sir Mike Jackson</a> and General <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Clark" title="Wesley Clark">Wesley Clark</a> over <a href="/wiki/Incident_at_Pristina_airport" title="Incident at Pristina airport">KFOR actions at Pristina Airport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gsmjdt_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-gsmjdt-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>NATO commanders can issue orders to their subordinate commanders in the form of operational plans (OPLANs), operational orders (OPORDERs), tactical direction, or fragmental orders (FRAGOs) and others. The joint rules of engagement must be followed, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_of_Armed_Conflict" title="Law of Armed Conflict">Law of Armed Conflict</a> must be obeyed at all times. Operational resources "remain under national command but have been transferred temporarily to NATO. Although these national units, through the formal process of transfer of authority, have been placed under the operational command and control of a NATO commander, they never lose their national character." Senior national representatives, like <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Defence_Staff_(disambiguation)" title="Chief of the Defence Staff (disambiguation)">CDS</a>, "are designated as so-called red-cardholders". Caveats are restrictions listed "nation by nation... that NATO Commanders... must take into account."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-terla_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-terla-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
